тАШ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рди рдпрдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдирд╡рд░реНрдЪрдореЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреИрд░реНрдШрддрдорд╕рдВ рдЬрд╛рдЧрддрдВ рдореИрддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгрдореН ред рдЖрджреНрдпрд╛ рдореИрддреНрд░реНрдпреЗрд╡ ред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рдордгрд┐рдХрд╛ – рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рдирд╡ рдореИрддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгрдВ рд╣рд┐ рдЬрд╛рдЧрддрдВ рдореИрддреНрд░реНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

151
Mitra and Varun╠гa
D─лrghatamas Aucathya
9 verses: jagat─л
The second part of this hymn (vss. 6cd through 9) is fairly straightforward, depict ing Mitra and Varuс╣Зa as the focus of the sacrifice and the patrons of the sacrificer. The first part is a different storyтАФenigmatic in reference and convoluted in expres sion. However, it appears to concern the same topic: Mitra and Varuс╣ЗaтАЩs presence at and participation in the sacrifice. We can therefore think of the hymn as an example of large-scale тАЬpoetic repair,тАЭ with the second part rephrasing the first in less con torted expressions. (On poetic repair see Jamison 2006.)
The hymn begins with the birth of Agni, presented both as ritual fire and as formidable god. The first half of verse 1 places the birth at the sacrifice itself, тАЬamid the cows and the waters,тАЭ in our opinion referring to the two auxiliary substances necessary for soma preparation, the milk for mixing and the water for rinsing and diluting. But in the second half of the verse the birth causes cosmic consternation, with the two worlds set atremble by his size and his тАЬsong,тАЭ presumably a reference to the crackling of a blazing fire.
Mitra and Varuс╣Зa make their appearance in verse 2, as sacrificial partners of a named soma-offerer; they are brought to the ritual ground and urged to aid the ritual participants. But the theme of birth returns in verse 3. Contrary to most interpretations, we consider the birth in question to be AgniтАЩs birth, treated already in verse 1, not the birth of Mitra and Varuс╣Зa. (The dual pronoun v─Бm in 3a is in WackernagelтАЩs Position, and we construe it later in the verse, as often.) As in verse 1, humans assist at the birth of the ritual fire, a birth that has cosmic resonances. Mitra and Varuс╣Зa also assist, bringing their skill to bear for the sacrifice (here referred to as тАЬtruthтАЭ [r╠еt├б]) and the fire. Their contributions to the sacrifice are also treated in verse 4; the skill mentioned in verse 3 they bring from heaven (4c), while they also make ready the soma-preparing waters mentioned in verse 1 (4d). Soma preparation is also the subject of the next verse (5). The cows (that is, their milk) are depicted turbulently milling around the ritual ground, bellowing at the three times of day associated with soma-pressingтАФdawn, midday, and sunset. (It should be noted that vs. 5 is the most puzzling verse in the hymn, and our interpretation does not entirely match those of others scholars.) In the first half of verse 6 we return to the ritual fire, kindled in verse 1тАФor rather to its flames, conceived of as тАЬlong-haired females.тАЭ (The poet, D─лrghatamas, uses the same image and the same word in I.140.8, where the reference to flames is clearer.)

As mentioned above, the highly wrought and cryptic treatment of the sacrifice and Mitra and Varuс╣ЗaтАЩs place in it is succeeded, starting with the second half of verse 6, by a fairly uncomplex restatement of the major themes.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Mitra and Varuс╣Зa The published introduction. gives a conspectus of the hymn, esp. the difficult first 5 vss.

рдпреЛрдЬрдиреАрдпрдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHeaven and earth have been terrified by the strength and the noise (of him), whom pious worshippers, desirous of acquiring cattle, have genitive rated by their (sacred) acts, amidst the waters (of the firmament), at the sacrifice, as a friend for the preservation of living beings, the benefactor (of man), and entitled to adoration.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As a friend: mitram na: Agni is compared to a friend; Mitram is identified with Agni of the firmament, or lightning].

Jamison Brereton

Whom [=Agni] like an ally [/Mitra] those very attentive ones, seeking cattle, begot with energy at the ceremony amid the cows and the
watersтАФ
the two world-halves trembled by reason of his dimensions and his song, in confronting him, the dear help of (all) the races, worthy of the
sacrifice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For the ritual application of the various portions of this vs. see published introduction.

Most tr. take g├│с╣гu and also perhaps aps├║ as the desired objects of battle (e.g., Geldner тАЬ(im Kampf) um die RinderтАЭ), but these seem to me to refer rather to the accoutrements of the soma sacrifice. The cows and the waters reappear in ritual context (at least in my view) in 4d and 5b respectively.

The standard tr. also supply a verb with p─Бda d, but this seems unnecessary.

Griffith

HEAVEN and earth trembled at the might and voice of him, whom, loved and Holy One, helper of all mankind,
The wise who longed for spoil in fight for kine brought forth with power, a Friend, mid waters, at the sacrifice.

Geldner

Den wie einen Freund die Rinderbegehrenden mit Eifer im Kampf um die Rinder, in guter Absicht unter weiser Rede im Wasser erzeugten - es erbebten beide Welten ├╝ber seine Erscheinung, seine Stimme; sie kamen dem lieben, opferw├╝rdigen Hort der Gesch├╢pfe freundlich entgegen.

Grassmann

Den durch ihr Werk wie einen Freund die eifrigen beim Fest nach K├╝hen strebend zeugten in der Luft, Vor seinem Glanz und Rauschen bebt das Weltenpaar, des lieben, heil’gen, der der Wesen Sch├╝tzer ist.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬSince they, (the priests), like friends, have prepared for you both, (Mitra and Varuс╣Зa a libation) of the abundantly-flowing and spontaneous Soma, therefore do you consent to come to the rite of the worshipper, and listen, showerers (of blessings), to the (prayers of the) householdeс╣ЫтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Abundantly flowing: alternative rendering: purum─лс╕╖hasya sominaс╕е = Soma offering Purum─лс╕╖ha, a prince

Jamison Brereton

Just now when the associates of Purum─лс╕Нha the soma-offerer, like allies [/Mitras], have brought you two forward,
now find the will and the way for the one who chants, and listen to the possessor of the dwelling place, you two bulls.

Griffith

As these, like friends, have done this work for you, these prompt servants of Purumilha Soma-offerer,
Give mental power to him who sings the sacred song, and hearken, Strong Ones, to the master of the house.

Geldner

Da euch beiden jetzt die guten Gehilfen des somafeiernden Purumilha wie Freunde den Vorzug bei dem Opfer gegeben haben, so findet Rat und Weg f├╝r den Preisenden und erh├╢ret, ihr Bullen, den Ruf des Hausherrn!

Grassmann

Wenn diesen Trunk des Purumidha Diener hier, des Somabringers, euch als Freunde vorgesetzt, So gebt Gesang dem Dichter und Begeisterung, und h├╢rt auf den, o Helden, der im Hause weilt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFor the sake (of obtaining) great vigour, showerers (of benefits), men glorify your birth from heaven and earth, which is to be extolled, inasmuch as you bestow (his desires) upon the worshipper (as the reward) of his sacrifice, and accept the rite (that is solemnized) with praise and oblation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Your birth from heaven and earth: v─Бm janma rodasyoс╕е = yuvayoс╕е sambandhi janma jananam utpattim, dy─Бvapс╣Ыthivyoс╕е saka┼Ы─Бt, the birth connected with you two from heaven and earth

Jamison Brereton

The settlements attended upon (his) birth, which was worthy to be proclaimed in the two world-halves, for the sake of your great skill,
o bulls.
When you bring it [=skill] for truth, when for the steed [=Agni?], with the oblation you energetically pursue the rite.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, I consider the birth described here to be that of Agni (as throughout the rest of D─лrghatamasтАЩs corpus and esp. in vs. 1 of this hymn), not of Mitra and Varuс╣Зa (with the standard tr.). I construe the Wackernagelpositioned v─Бm with d├бkс╣гase in b. This d├бkс╣гas- is then the referent of ─лm in c.

I also take c as subordinated to d (with Renou), not ab (with the others). That both c and d have 2nd du. pres. verbs (bh├бrathaс╕е тАж v─лthaс╕е) is suggestive, and the present in c does not work very well with the mythological past in ab.

Griffith

The folk have glorified your birth from Earth and Heaven, to be extolled, ye Strong Ones, for your mighty power.
Ye, when ye bring to singer and the rite, enjoy the sacrifice performed with holy praise and strength.

Geldner

Die Menschenv├╢lker feiern euer beider Geburt, die preisenswerte, die beiden Welten zu gro├Яem Erfolg gereicht, ihr Bullen, da ihr ihn dem Gesetz und dem Rennpferd bringt. Durch die Spende und den eifrigen Dienst bekommt ihr Lust zum Opfer.

Grassmann

Euch Helden beide r├╝steten zu grosser Kraft der beiden Welten preisenswerthe St├дmme aus; Was ihr dem Priester und was ihr dem S├дnger bringt, durch frommes Werk und Ruf belebt das Opfer ihr.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPowerful divinities, most acceptable to you both is that spot, (where you are worshipped); accepters of sacrifice, proclaim the great ceremony (as duly performed); for you two connect the efficacious and comprehensive rise with the vast heaven, like a cow with a burden.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

You two connect: divo bс╣Ыhato dakс╣гam ─Бbhuvam g─Бm na dhuri upayu├▒j─Бthe apas, you two join the work (apas) able (to support the burden) of heaven, and applying to all creatures, as a cow to a load; the allusion is to the adequacy of worship or sacrifice to effect its objects, or realize its rewards, as the cow is able to bear a burden suited to her bodily strength: dhur─л┼Ы─Бr─лrabalasya nirv─Бhe tad artham g─Бm na dhenum iva; or, the allusion may be to her ability to give milk and the rest, kс╣г─лr─Бdikam iva

Jamison Brereton

It is the settlement greatly dear (to you) that (gets) ahead, o lord(s)тАФo truthful ones, you two loudly sound your lofty truthтАФ
You (hitch up) your skill from lofty heaven (to be) ready at hand; you hitch up the waters like an ox to a yoke-pole.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The voc. asura with short final probably stands for the expected dual asur─Б (so read in the Pp. and accepted by the standard tr. and AiG III.53), though it is barely possible that only Varuс╣Зa (or Mitra) is addressed. The numerous duals (с╣Ы╠Бt─Бv─Бnau, ghoс╣гathaс╕е, yuv├бm, yu├▒j─Бthe) make this unlikely.

I consider the d├бkс╣гam in c to be Mitra and Varuс╣ЗaтАЩs (like the d├бkс╣гas- of vs. 3) and take div├│ bс╣Ыhat├бс╕е as an abl. of source: тИЪyuj + abl. тАШyoke fromтАЩ is a fairly common idiom.

Renou takes ap├бс╕е in d as тАШlaborтАЩ (тАЬlтАЩoeuvre (sacr├йe)тАЭ), but the accent is of course wrong. Moreover, as indicated in comm. to vs. 1, the waters here make a pair with the cows of 5b, both as ritual substances.

Griffith

The people prospers, Asuras! whom ye dearly love: ye, Righteous Ones, proclaim aloud the Holy Law.
That efficacious power that comes from lofty heaven, ye bind unto the work, as to the pole an ox.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou bring (the cattle) to their acceptable (pasture) upon earth, whence the milk-yielding cows, protected by your power, return unharmed to their stalls; they cry to the sun (in heaven) above, both at evening and at dawn, as one (cries aloud) who detects a thief.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Like) the two great (world-halves) in their greatness you two propel the desirable reward here. The milk-cows, pushing and shoving (though) not raising dust, are at the (ritual) seat.
They cry out to the sun at its zenith (and) up to its setting (and) through the dawns, like a bird (screeching) in swooping pursuit.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. take mah─л╠Бin p─Бda a as a loc sg. (Geldner тАШauf ErdenтАЩ). Since loc. sg. -─л is extremely rare, I prefer to take it as the du. nom./acc. it appears to be, referring to the two world halves (see r├│das─л in 1c) in an unmarked simile.

In b the root noun t├║jaс╕е is grammaticaly ambiguous; with Grassmann, Geldner, Witzel Got┼Н, Schindler (RtNoun) I take it as nom. pl., against Renou (gen. sg.). (Oldenberg considers both nom. and acc. pl., without deciding.) The image, in my view, is of a herd of cows milling around in confusion on the ritual ground, but not raising dust as a real herd would do – because, after all, the тАЬcowsтАЭ are really milk.

In cd, following RenouтАЩs interpr., I see reference to the times of the three soma pressings. With Renou I tr. upar├бt─Бti as zenith, referring to the sunтАЩs position at the Midday Pressing; ─Б╠Бnimr├║caс╕е is an abl. with ─Б╠БтАЬuntil its setting,тАЭ referring to the Third (or evening) Pressing. Unlike Renou I do not take uс╣г├бsaс╕е as тАШ├а lтАЩauroreтАЩ (as if a loc. sg.), but rather as an acc. of extent of time, тАЬthrough the dawns,тАЭ though an abl. sg.

with the preceding ─Б╠Б(Geldner тАЬ(bis) zum MorgenтАЭ) might be possible – in any case, a ref.

to the Morning Pressing.

On takvav─л╠Б- see also I.134.5. The stem occurs also in X.91.2, which is perhaps the passage in which the тАШbirdтАЩ sense is the clearest. Although тАШswoopingly/swiftly pursuingтАЩ need not have a bird as its referent, and in our passage here the standard tr.

take it as simply a pursuer (presumably human; e.g., Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н] Verfolger), I am inclined to take it as a bird of prey rather than simply a hunter, because takt├б (and other тИЪtak forms) seem to be used esp. of birds and beasts considered to be like them; see comm. ad IX.32.4. In our passage the point of comparison between the cows in the frame and the takvav─л╠Б- has to be the crying out (sv├бranti), which fits the sharp squawking of birds of prey, but not the general behavior of human hunters.

Griffith

On this great earth ye send your treasure down with might: unstained by dust, the crowding kine are in the stalls.
Here in the neighbourhood they cry unto the Sun at morning and at evening, like swift birds of prey.

Geldner

Hier auf Erden erf├╝llet ihr durch eure Macht den Wunsch: Staublose, ungeduldige Milchk├╝he sind in eurem Wohnsitz. Diese br├╝llen hinter der Sonne her bis zum Abend, bis zum Morgen wie der Verfolger eines R├дubers.

Grassmann

Auf diese Erde sendet Gut in F├╝lle ihr; staublose, t├╝cht’ge K├╝he stehen in dem Stall; Das Sonnenlicht umrauschen in der N├дhe sie vom Morgen bis zum Abend schnellen Falken gleich.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe tresses of Agni minister, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, to your sacrifice, when you honour (with your presence) the sacrificial chamber; send down of your own accord (the rain), and prosper our offerings, for you have command over the praise of the pious men.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The long-haired females [=flames] have bellowed to you for truth, where [=ritual seat] you are chanting the way, o Mitra, o Varuс╣Зa.
Send (them) surging down by yourselves; swell our insights: you two have control over the thoughts of the inspired poet.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda-final g─Бt├║m ├бrcathaс╕е seems to echo likewise p─Бda-final g─Бt├║m ├бrcata in 2c, but in fact, at least according to me and the other standard tr., the similarity is misleading. In our passage g─Бt├║m is surely the object of du. pres. ├бrcathaс╕е, but in 2c g─Б╠Бt├║m is better taken as the object of the preceding verb vidatam, and ├бrcata in sandhi before ut├б, which opens the next p─Бda, is better taken as having the underlying form ├бrcate (so Pp.), the dat. sg. act. participle, rather than du. injunc. ├бrcataс╕е, which is technically possible. This teasing but false superimposibility seems the opposite of тАЬpoetic repairтАЭ – тАЬpoetic breakageтАЭ perhaps?

Griffith

The flames with curling tresses serve your sacrifice, whereto ye sing the song, Mitra and Varuna.
Send down of your free will, prosper our holy songs: ye are sole Masters of the singer’s hymn of praise.

Geldner

Die Langhaarigen schrieen eurem Gesetz zu, w├дhrend ihr, Mitra und Varuna, den Weg vorsinget. Entbindet selbst, befruchtet die Gedanken! Ihr leitet das Dichten des Redekundigen.

Grassmann

Zu eurem Opfer haben, Mitra-Varuna, gerauscht die lock’gen Flammen, wo eur Lied ert├╢nt; Ges├дnge giesset selbst herab und segnet sie; ihr gebt die Richtung dem Gebet des Preisenden.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬCome to the devout (worshipper), who, glorifying you, and providing (all that is) acceptable, presents you with oblations; (to him), the sage, the invoker, who offers you worship; accept his sacrifice; favourably disposed towards us, (accept) our praises.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(The man) who as he labors piously serves you with sacrifices, the poet and Hotar who performs the sacrifice, bringing his thoughts to
successтАФ
itтАЩs him that you come near; you pursue his rite. Seeking us, come here to our songs and our good thinking.

Jamison Brereton Notes

v─лth├│ adhvar├бm exactly matches v─лtho adhvar├бm in 3d (save for the accent).

Here, unlike the false identity in vs. 6 just discussed, the phrases have identical sense and reference.

In b the nominatives kav├нс╕е and h├│t─Б seem each appropriate to one part of the rest of the p─Бda: the poet to manmas─Б╠Бdhanaс╕е and the Hotar-priest to y├бjati. RenouтАЩs tr., with his trademark verbosity, makes this division of labor explicit.

Griffith

Whoso with sacrifices toiling brings you gifts, and worships, sage and priest, fulfilling your desire,–
To him do ye draw nigh and taste his sacrifice. Come well-inclined to us unto our songs and prayer.

Geldner

Wer euch mit Opfer dient und spendet, als weiser Hotri opfert und das Gedicht richtig durchf├╝hrt, den suchet ihr auf und bekommt Lust zu seinem Opfer. Kommet zu unserer Lobrede, zu der Huldigung uns zugetan!

Grassmann

Wer euch durch Opfer eifrig wirkend huldiget, als weiser Priester euch verehrt, Gebete spricht, Zu dem erscheint ihr und geniesst den Opfertrank; kommt holdgesinnt zu unserm Liede und Gebet.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAccepter of sacrifices, you are the first whom (worshippers) propitiate with offerings, the produce of the cow; like (the application) of the mind (in the first instrumental nce) to the results (of the senses); hymns (prompted) by thoughts wholly intent upon you, celebrate (your praise); do you, with humble minds, bestow upon us wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They anoint you first with sacrifices and with cows. O truthful ones, as if at the yoking of mind
they bring you songs along with uninterrupted thought. With
undistracted mind you have attained rich (vigor).

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take b with c, rather than with a as do the standard tr., since тАЬthe yoking of mind,тАЭ whatever it may precisely mean, harmonizes better with the thought, songs, and mind of the rest of the verse than with the more physical manifestation of the sacrifice in p─Бda a. As for the meaning of the phrase, I assume that it is part of the larger conceptual complex likening the sacrifice and its various elements to a chariot and its associated elements. The yoking or harnessing of mind refers to embarking on concentrated and deliberate mental effort for the sake of the sacrifice. Cf. Mitra and Varuс╣ЗaтАЩs yoking of their skill in 4cd.

тАЬYoking of mindтАЭ actually contains the pl. pr├бyuktiс╣гu, but the pl. form is probably the result of a mechanical metrical adjustment: m├бnaso n├б pr├бyukti (shortvowel instr.) is found at p─Бda end in X.30.1 in a Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence, and this phrase was converted into a Jagat─л cadence here by the addition of -su. The other two occurrences of the stem pr├бyukti- are likewise p─Бda-final in Triс╣гс╣нubh and end in -ti(с╕е).

One of these, тАж n├б pr├бyuktiс╕е, is found two hymns after this one, in I.153.2, where I (so also Renou) take the phrase as abbreviated from *m├бnaso n├б pr├бyukti-, as here.

Griffith

With sacrifices and with milk they deck you first, ye Righteous Ones, as if through stirrings of the mind.
To you they bring their hymns with their collected thought, while ye with earnest soul come to us gloriously.

Geldner

Euch salben sie zuerst mit Opfern, mit den Gaben der Kuh, ihr Gesetzestreuen, wie auf eigenen Antrieb des Herzens. Sie bringen euch Lieder dar gesammelten Geistes. Mit besonnenem Sinn habt ihr reiche Kraft erlangt!

Grassmann

Durch Opfer und durch Tr├дnke schm├╝cken euch zuerst die frommgesinnten, wie getrieben durch den Geist; Sie bringen euch mit stetem Sinnen Lieder dar, und reichlich kommt achtsamen Geistes ihr herbei.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou distribute food, accompanied by riches; you bestow upon us, leaders (of sacrifice), wealth, ample, and defended by your wise provisions; the days with the nights have not attained your divinity; neither have the rivers, nor have the asuras, and they have not obtained (your) wealth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The days with the nights: dy─Бvo ahabhir na: dy─Бv─Бс╕е = days;

Ahan = night; have not attained your divinity: n─Бna┼Ыurmagham: ─Бna┼Ыuс╕е pr─Бpnuvanti na v─Бm dy─Бvo, i.e, there is no one in the three worlds more powerful than Mitra and Varuс╣Зa: lokatraye yuvayoс╕е par─Бbhavit─Бro na ke api santi

Jamison Brereton

You have acquired rich vigor; you have attained itтАФrich, great, and enduringтАФwith your magic arts. Through the days neither the heavens nor the rivers have attained your divinity, nor the Paс╣Зis your bounty.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The voc. n├бr─Б in b was carelessly omitted in the published translation Insert тАЬo superior men.тАЭ3 In c the phrase dy─Б╠Бv├│ тАЩhabhiс╕е is rendered тАЬthe days with their daytimesтАЭ by all standard tr. However, although there are undeniable instances of pl. dy─Б╠Бvaс╕е meaning тАШdaysтАЩ (e.g., VI.24.7, 38.4) and ├бhabhiс╕е is suggestive, I prefer тАШheavensтАЩ, which is the more common meaning of nom. dy─Б╠Бvaс╕е. I.130.10 ├бhobhir iva dya├║с╕е, with the nom. sg., where тАШheavenтАЩ is the only possible interpr., supports тАШheavensтАЩ here. The context of our passage gives no help either way: dy─Б╠Бvaс╕е is conjoined with s├нndhavaс╕е тАШriversтАЩ, which would not seem to form a natural class either with тАШheavensтАЩ or with тАШdaysтАЩ (though see Klein, DGRV 2.144 for other exx. of тАШheavenтАЩ conjoined with waters of some sort), and the statements тАЬthe heavens have not attained your divinityтАЭ and тАЬthe days have not attained your divinityтАЭ are almost equally puzzling – though IтАЩd give the edge of sense of the former.

Griffith

Rich strength of life is yours: ye, Heroes, have obtained through your surpassing powers rich far-extending might.
Not the past days conjoined with nights, not rivers, not the Panis have attained your Godhead and your wealth.

Geldner

Ihr besitzet reiche Kraft, ihr habt reiche Kraft erlangt, ihr Herren, durch eure Zauberkr├дfte, sofort helfende, gewaltige. Nicht konnten die Tage mit den Tageszeiten, noch die Str├╢me es eurer Gottheit gleichtun, noch die Pani┬┤s eurem Reichtum.

Grassmann

Ihr gebet und empfanget reichlich frische Kraft, durch Zaubermacht, o M├дnner, stete Herrlichkeit, Nicht haben Himmel, Tage, noch die Str├╢me, noch D├дmonen eure Gottheit euren Reichthum je erreicht.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдирд░рд╛ рдпреМ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдВ рдорд╛рдпрд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрдорд╛рд╣рд┐рдирдорд┐рддрдКрддрд┐ рд╡рдпреЛ рд░реЗрд╡рджреНрджрдзрд╛рдереЗ рд░реЗрд╡рджрд╛рд╢рд╛рдереЗ рдЪ рддрдпреЛрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВ рджреЗрд╡рддреНрд╡рдВ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡реЛ рдирд╛рд╣рднрд┐рд░рд╣рд╛рдирд┐ рдиреЛрдд рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзрд╡реЛ рдирд╛рдирд╢реБрдГ рдкрдгрдпреЛ рдордШрдВ рдЪ рдирд╛рдирд╢реБрдГ рее реп рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд░реЗрд╡рддреН) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрдзрдирд╡рддреН (рд╡рдпрдГ) рдХрдордиреАрдпрдореН (рджрдзрд╛рдереЗ) рдзрд░рдердГ (рд░реЗрд╡рддреН) рдмрд╣реНрд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН (рдЖрд╢рд╛рдереЗ) (рдирд░рд╛) рдирд╛рдпрдХреМ (рдорд╛рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рднрд┐рдГ (рдЗрддрдКрддрд┐) рдЗрддрдГ рдКрддрд┐рдГ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рддрддреН (рдорд╛рд╣рд┐рдирдореН) рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдВ рдкреВрдЬреНрдпрдВ рдорд╣рдЪреНрдЪред рдорд╛рд╣рд┐рди рдЗрддрд┐ рдорд╣рдиреНрдирд╛режред рдирд┐рдШрдВреж рейред рейред (рди) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рд╡рд╛рдореН) рдпреБрд╡рдпреЛрдГ (рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рдГ (рдЕрд╣рднрд┐рдГ) рджрд┐рдиреИрдГ (рди) (рдЙрдд) (рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзрд╡рдГ) рдирджреНрдпрдГ (рди) (рджреЗрд╡рддреНрд╡рдореН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрддреНрд╡рдореН (рдкрдгрдпрдГ) рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд░рдорд╛рдгрд╛рдГ (рди) (рдЖрдирд╢реБрдГ) рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ (рдордШрдореН) рдорд╣рджреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдореН рее реп рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ
